   <h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Smartphone</h1> 
   <div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content"> 
    <div id="siteSub">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div> 
    <div id="contentSub">
     <div id="mw-fr-revisiontag" class="flaggedrevs_short plainlinks noprint nomobile">
      <div class="flaggedrevs_short_basic">

     <div role="note" class="hatnote">

     <div role="note" class="hatnote">
      Not to be confused with 
      <a href="/wiki/Feature_phone" title="Feature phone">Feature phone</a>.
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:IPhone_5S_home_button.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/IPhone_5S_home_button.png/220px-IPhone_5S_home_button.png" width="220" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/IPhone_5S_home_button.png/330px-IPhone_5S_home_button.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/IPhone_5S_home_button.png/440px-IPhone_5S_home_button.png 2x" data-file-width="3953" data-file-height="2767"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:IPhone_5S_home_button.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> An 
        <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple</a> 
        <a href="/wiki/IPhone_5S" title="IPhone 5S">iPhone 5S</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>A <b>smartphone</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Mobile_phone" title="Mobile phone">mobile phone</a> with an advanced <a href="/wiki/Mobile_operating_system" title="Mobile operating system">mobile operating system</a> which combines features of a <a href="/wiki/Personal_computer" title="Personal computer">personal computer</a> operating system with other features useful for mobile or handheld use.<sup id="cite_ref-phonescoop-smartphone_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-phonescoop-smartphone-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-phonescoop-featurephone_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-phonescoop-featurephone-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> They typically combine the features of a cell phone with those of other popular <a href="/wiki/Mobile_device" title="Mobile device">mobile devices</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Personal_digital_assistant" title="Personal digital assistant">personal digital assistant</a> (PDA), <a href="/wiki/Portable_media_player" title="Portable media player">media player</a> and <a href="/wiki/GPS_navigation_device#Mobile_phones_with_GPS_hapability" title="GPS navigation device">GPS navigation unit</a>. Most smartphones can access the <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">Internet</a>, have a <a href="/wiki/Touchscreen" title="Touchscreen">touchscreen</a> <a href="/wiki/User_interface" title="User interface">user interface</a>, with either an LCD, OLED, AMOLED, LED or similar screen, can run third-party <a href="/wiki/Mobile_app" title="Mobile app">apps</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portable_media_player" title="Portable media player">music players</a> and are <a href="/wiki/Camera_phone" title="Camera phone">camera phones</a>. Most smartphones produced from 2012 onwards also have high-speed mobile broadband <a href="/wiki/LTE_(telecommunication)" title="LTE (telecommunication)">4G LTE</a> <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">internet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Motion_detector" title="Motion detector">motion sensors</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mobile_payment" title="Mobile payment">mobile payment</a>.</p> 
     <p></p>

     <p></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_years">Early years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Caller_ID_receiver.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Caller_ID_receiver.jpg/220px-Caller_ID_receiver.jpg" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Caller_ID_receiver.jpg/330px-Caller_ID_receiver.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Caller_ID_receiver.jpg/440px-Caller_ID_receiver.jpg 2x" data-file-width="680" data-file-height="474"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Caller_ID_receiver.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> The first caller identification receiver (1971).
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Devices that combined telephony and <a href="/wiki/Computing" title="Computing">computing</a> were first conceptualized by <a href="/wiki/Nikola_Tesla" title="Nikola Tesla">Nikola Tesla</a> in 1909 and <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Paraskevakos" title="Theodore Paraskevakos">Theodore Paraskevakos</a> in 1971 and patented in 1974, and were offered for sale beginning in 1993. Paraskevakos was the first to introduce the concepts of intelligence, <a href="/wiki/Data_processing" title="Data processing">data processing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Visual_display_screen" title="Visual display screen" class="mw-redirect">visual display screens</a> into telephones. In 1971, while he was working with <a href="/wiki/Boeing" title="Boeing">Boeing</a> in <a href="/wiki/Huntsville,_Alabama" title="Huntsville, Alabama">Huntsville, Alabama</a>, Paraskevakos demonstrated a <a href="/wiki/Transmitter" title="Transmitter">transmitter</a> and <a href="/wiki/Receiver_(radio)" title="Receiver (radio)" class="mw-redirect">receiver</a> that provided additional ways to communicate with remote equipment, however it did not yet have general purpose <a href="/wiki/PDA" title="PDA" class="mw-redirect">PDA</a> applications in a wireless device typical of smartphones. They were installed at Peoples' Telephone Company in <a href="/wiki/Leesburg,_Alabama" title="Leesburg, Alabama">Leesburg, Alabama</a> and were demonstrated to several telephone companies. The original and historic working models are still in the possession of Paraskevakos.<sup id="cite_ref-paraskevakos_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-paraskevakos-4">[4]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Forerunner">Forerunner</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Forerunner">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:IBM_Simon_Personal_Communicator.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/IBM_Simon_Personal_Communicator.png/170px-IBM_Simon_Personal_Communicator.png" width="170" height="316" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/IBM_Simon_Personal_Communicator.png/255px-IBM_Simon_Personal_Communicator.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/IBM_Simon_Personal_Communicator.png/340px-IBM_Simon_Personal_Communicator.png 2x" data-file-width="1615" data-file-height="3000"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:IBM_Simon_Personal_Communicator.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/IBM_Simon" title="IBM Simon">IBM Simon</a> and charging base (1994).
        <sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The first mobile phone to incorporate PDA features was an <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a> prototype developed in 1992 and demonstrated that year at the <a href="/wiki/COMDEX" title="COMDEX">COMDEX</a> computer industry trade show. The prototype demonstrated PDA features as well as other visionary apps like maps, stocks and news incorporated with a cellular phone. A refined version of the product was marketed to consumers in 1994 by <a href="/wiki/BellSouth" title="BellSouth">BellSouth</a> under the name <a href="/wiki/IBM_Simon" title="IBM Simon">Simon Personal Communicator</a>. The Simon was the first cellular device that can be properly referred to as a "smartphone", although it was not called that in 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-bus_week_2012_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bus_week_2012-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-schneidawind_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schneidawind-7">[7]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBC_News_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_News-8">[8]</a></sup> In addition to its ability to make and receive cellular phone calls, Simon was able to send and receive <a href="/wiki/Faxes" title="Faxes" class="mw-redirect">faxes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Emails" title="Emails" class="mw-redirect">emails</a> and included several other apps like address book, calendar, appointment scheduler, calculator, world time clock, and note pad through its touch screen display. Simon is the first smartphone to be incorporated with the features of a PDA.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The term "smart phone" first appeared in print in 1995, for describing AT&amp;T's "PhoneWriter Communicator" as a "smart phone".<sup id="cite_ref-ACM_Interactions_article_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ACM_Interactions_article-10">[10]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="PDAs">PDAs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: PDAs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Personal_digital_assistant" title="Personal digital assistant">Personal digital assistant</a>
     </div> 
     <p>In the late 1990s, many mobile phone users carried a separate dedicated PDA device, running early versions of operating systems such as <a href="/wiki/Palm_OS" title="Palm OS">Palm OS</a>, <a href="/wiki/BlackBerry_OS" title="BlackBerry OS">BlackBerry OS</a> or <a href="/wiki/Windows_CE" title="Windows CE">Windows CE</a>/<a href="/wiki/Pocket_PC" title="Pocket PC">Pocket PC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-phonescoop-smartphone_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-phonescoop-smartphone-1">[1]</a></sup> These operating systems would later evolve into <a href="/wiki/Mobile_operating_system" title="Mobile operating system">mobile operating systems</a>.</p> 
     <p>In March 1996, <a href="/wiki/Hewlett-Packard" title="Hewlett-Packard">Hewlett-Packard</a> released the <a href="/wiki/OmniGo_700LX" title="OmniGo 700LX" class="mw-redirect">OmniGo 700LX</a>, which was a modified <a href="/wiki/200LX" title="200LX" class="mw-redirect">200LX</a> PDA that supported a Nokia 2110-compatible phone and had integrated software built in ROM to support it. The device featured a 640x200 resolution CGA compatible 4-shade gray-scale LCD screen and could be used to make and receive calls, text messages, emails and faxes. It was also 100% DOS 5.0 compatible, allowing it to run thousands of existing software titles including early versions of Windows.</p> 
     <p>In August 1996, <a href="/wiki/Nokia" title="Nokia">Nokia</a> released the <a href="/wiki/Nokia_9000_Communicator" title="Nokia 9000 Communicator">Nokia 9000 Communicator</a> which combined a PDA based on the <a href="/wiki/GEOS_V3.0" title="GEOS V3.0" class="mw-redirect">GEOS V3.0</a> operating system from <a href="/wiki/Geoworks" title="Geoworks" class="mw-redirect">Geoworks</a> with a digital cellular phone based on the <a href="/wiki/Nokia_2110" title="Nokia 2110">Nokia 2110</a>. The two devices were fixed together via a hinge in what became known as a <a href="/wiki/Clamshell_design" title="Clamshell design" class="mw-redirect">clamshell design</a>. When opened, the display was on the inside top surface and with a physical <a href="/wiki/QWERTY_keyboard" title="QWERTY keyboard" class="mw-redirect">QWERTY keyboard</a> on the bottom. The personal organizer provided e-mail, calendar, address book, calculator and notebook with text-based web browsing, and the ability to send and receive faxes. When the personal organizer was closed, it could be used as a digital cellular phone.</p> 
     <p>In June 1999, <a href="/wiki/Qualcomm" title="Qualcomm">Qualcomm</a> released a "CDMA Digital PCS Smartphone" with integrated Palm PDA and Internet connectivity, known as the "pdQ Smartphone".<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>In early 2000, the <a href="/wiki/Ericsson_R380" title="Ericsson R380">Ericsson R380</a> was released by <a href="/wiki/Ericsson_Mobile_Communications" title="Ericsson Mobile Communications">Ericsson Mobile Communications</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> and was the first device marketed as a "smartphone".<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> It combined the functions of a mobile phone and a PDA, supported limited web browsing with a <a href="/wiki/Resistive_touchscreen" title="Resistive touchscreen">resistive touchscreen</a> utilizing a <a href="/wiki/Stylus_(computing)" title="Stylus (computing)">stylus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>In early 2001, <a href="/wiki/Palm,_Inc." title="Palm, Inc.">Palm, Inc.</a> introduced the <a href="/wiki/Kyocera_6035" title="Kyocera 6035">Kyocera 6035</a>, which combined a PDA with a mobile phone and operated on <a href="/wiki/Verizon_Wireless" title="Verizon Wireless">Verizon</a>. It also supported limited web browsing.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 2002, <a href="/wiki/Handspring_(company)" title="Handspring (company)">Handspring</a> released the <a href="/wiki/Treo_180" title="Treo 180">Treo 180</a>, the first smartphone to combine <a href="/wiki/Palm_OS" title="Palm OS">Palm OS</a> and a GSM phone, with telephony, SMS messaging and Internet access fully integrated into Palm OS.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Smartphones before Android, iOS and BlackBerry, typically ran on <a href="/wiki/Symbian" title="Symbian">Symbian</a>, which was originally developed by <a href="/wiki/Psion_(computers)" title="Psion (computers)" class="mw-redirect">Psion</a>. It was the world's most widely used smartphone operating system until the last quarter of 2010.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mass_adoption">Mass adoption</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Mass adoption">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>In 1999, the Japanese firm <a href="/wiki/NTT_DoCoMo" title="NTT DoCoMo">NTT DoCoMo</a> released the first smartphones to achieve mass adoption within a country. These phones ran on <a href="/wiki/I-mode" title="I-mode">i-mode</a>, which provided data transmission speeds up to 9.6 kbit/s.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> Unlike future generations of wireless services, NTT DoCoMo's i-mode used <a href="/wiki/CHTML" title="CHTML" class="mw-redirect">cHTML</a>, a language which restricted some aspects of traditional <a href="/wiki/HTML" title="HTML">HTML</a> in favor of increasing data speed for the devices. Limited functionality, small screens and limited bandwidth allowed for phones to use the slower data speeds available.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>The rise of i-mode helped NTT DoCoMo accumulate an estimated 40 million subscribers by the end of 2001. It was also ranked first in market capitalization in Japan and second globally. This power would wane in the face of the rise of 3G and new phones with advanced wireless network capabilities.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Outside Japan smartphones were still rare until the introduction of the <a href="/wiki/Danger_Hiptop" title="Danger Hiptop">Danger Hiptop</a> in 2002, which saw moderate success in the US as the <a href="/wiki/T-Mobile" title="T-Mobile">T-Mobile</a> Sidekick. Later, in the mid-2000s, devices based on Microsoft's <a href="/wiki/Windows_Mobile" title="Windows Mobile">Windows Mobile</a> started to gain popularity among business users in the U.S. The <a href="/wiki/BlackBerry" title="BlackBerry">BlackBerry</a> later gained mass adoption in the U.S., and American users popularized the term "CrackBerry" in 2006 due to its addictive nature.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> The company first released its GSM BlackBerry 6210, BlackBerry 6220, and BlackBerry 6230 devices in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Symbian was the most popular smartphone OS in Europe during the middle to late 2000s. Initially, Nokia's Symbian devices were focused on business, similar to Windows Mobile and BlackBerry devices at the time. From 2006 onwards, Nokia started producing entertainment-focused smartphones, popularized by the <a href="/wiki/Nokia_Nseries" title="Nokia Nseries">Nseries</a>. In Asia, with the exception of Japan, the trend was similar to that of Europe.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="iOS.2C_Android_and_Windows_Phone">iOS, Android and Windows Phone</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: iOS, Android and Windows Phone">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>In early 2007, <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple Inc.</a> introduced the <a href="/wiki/IPhone_(original)" title="IPhone (original)" class="mw-redirect">iPhone</a>, one of the first smartphones to use a <a href="/wiki/Multi-touch" title="Multi-touch">multi-touch</a> interface. The iPhone was notable for its use of a large touchscreen for direct finger input as its main means of interaction, instead of a stylus, keyboard, or keypad typical for smartphones at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-iPhone-is-not_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iPhone-is-not-23">[23]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>In October 2008, the first phone to use <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a> called the <a href="/wiki/HTC_Dream" title="HTC Dream">HTC Dream</a> (also known as the T-Mobile G1) was released.<sup id="cite_ref-UK_release_of_T-Mobile_G1_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UK_release_of_T-Mobile_G1-24">[24]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-T-Mobile_G1_Event_Round-up_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-T-Mobile_G1_Event_Round-up-25">[25]</a></sup> Android is an <a href="/wiki/Open_source" title="Open source" class="mw-redirect">open-source</a> platform founded by <a href="/wiki/Andy_Rubin" title="Andy Rubin">Andy Rubin</a> and now owned by <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-open-alliance_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-open-alliance-26">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-android-atlas_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-android-atlas-27">[27]</a></sup> Although Android's adoption was relatively slow at first, it started to gain widespread popularity in 2010, and in early 2012 dominated the smartphone market share worldwide, which continues to this day.<sup id="cite_ref-Kantar_Worldpanel_Q3_2012_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kantar_Worldpanel_Q3_2012-28">[28]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>These new platforms led to the decline of earlier ones. <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a>, for instance, started a new OS from scratch, called <a href="/wiki/Windows_Phone" title="Windows Phone">Windows Phone</a>. Nokia abandoned Symbian and partnered with Microsoft to use Windows Phone on its smartphones. Windows Phone then became the third-most-popular OS. Palm's <a href="/wiki/WebOS" title="WebOS">webOS</a> was bought by Hewlett-Packard and later sold to <a href="/wiki/LG_Electronics" title="LG Electronics">LG Electronics</a> for use on LG <a href="/wiki/Smart_TV" title="Smart TV">smart TVs</a>. <a href="/wiki/BlackBerry_Limited" title="BlackBerry Limited">BlackBerry Limited</a>, formerly known as Research In Motion, also made a new platform based on <a href="/wiki/QNX" title="QNX">QNX</a>, <a href="/wiki/BlackBerry_10" title="BlackBerry 10">BlackBerry 10</a>.</p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Capacitive_touchscreen" title="Capacitive touchscreen" class="mw-redirect">capacitive touchscreen</a> also had a knock-on effect on smartphone <a href="/wiki/Form_factor_(mobile_phones)" title="Form factor (mobile phones)">form factors</a>. Before 2007, it was common for devices to have a physical numeric keypad or physical <a href="/wiki/QWERTY" title="QWERTY">QWERTY</a> keyboard in either a candybar or sliding form factor. However, by 2010, there were no top-selling smartphones with physical keypads.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_technological_developments">Recent technological developments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Recent technological developments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <ul> 
      <li>In 2013, the <a href="/wiki/Fairphone" title="Fairphone">Fairphone</a> company launched its first "socially ethical" smartphone at the <a href="/wiki/London_Design_Festival" title="London Design Festival">London Design Festival</a> to address concerns regarding the sourcing of materials in the manufacturing.<sup id="cite_ref-Fair_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fair-29">[29]</a></sup></li> 
      <li>In late 2013, QSAlpha commenced production of a smartphone designed entirely around security, encryption and identity protection.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></li> 
      <li>In December 2013, the world's first curved <a href="/wiki/OLED" title="OLED">OLED</a> technology smartphones were introduced to the retail market with the sale of the <a href="/wiki/Samsung_Galaxy_Round" title="Samsung Galaxy Round">Samsung Galaxy Round</a> and <a href="/wiki/LG_G_Flex" title="LG G Flex">LG G Flex</a> models.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> Samsung phones with more bends and folds in the screens were expected in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></li> 
      <li>In early 2014, smartphones were beginning to use <a href="/wiki/Quad_HD" title="Quad HD" class="mw-redirect">Quad HD</a> (2K) 2560x1440 on 5.5" screens with up to 534 <a href="/wiki/Pixel_density" title="Pixel density">PPI</a> on devices such as the <a href="/wiki/LG_G3" title="LG G3">LG G3</a> which is a significant improvement over Apple's <a href="/wiki/Retina_Display" title="Retina Display">Retina Display</a>. Quad HD is used in advanced televisions and computer monitors, but with 110 ppi or less on such larger displays.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></li> 
      <li>As of 2014, Wi-Fi networks were much used for smartphones. As Wi-Fi becomes more prevalent and easier to connect to, <a href="/wiki/Wi-Fi_phone" title="Wi-Fi phone" class="mw-redirect">Wi-Fi phone</a> services will start to take off.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></li> 
      <li>Smartphones are increasingly integrated with everyday uses. For instance, credit cards and mobile payments are integrated into smartphones where users can send cash payments through smartphone applications and SaaS platforms.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Recently, Apple Pay has picked up 34 new banks to the roster supporting their mobile payment platform, where merchants are rapidly adopting it.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Additionally, recent technological innovations are causing keys to be fused into the smartphones, where the smartphone can act as a digital key and access badge for its users.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></li> 
      <li>Since 2013, water and dustproofing have made their way into mainstream high end smartphones instead of specialty models with the <a href="/wiki/Sony_Xperia_Z" title="Sony Xperia Z">Sony Xperia Z</a> continuing through the <a href="/wiki/Sony_Xperia_Z3" title="Sony Xperia Z3">Sony Xperia Z3</a> and with the <a href="/wiki/Samsung_Galaxy_S5" title="Samsung Galaxy S5">Samsung Galaxy S5</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></li> 
      <li>LG introduced lasers on the LG G3 to help camera focus.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Lumia_950XL.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Lumia_950XL.jpg/220px-Lumia_950XL.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Lumia_950XL.jpg/330px-Lumia_950XL.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Lumia_950XL.jpg/440px-Lumia_950XL.jpg 2x" data-file-width="850" data-file-height="478"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Lumia_950XL.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Microsoft Lumia 950XL was the first phone to have 
        <i>Windows Continuum</i>
        <sup id="cite_ref-windows.microsoft.com_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-windows.microsoft.com-42">[42]</a></sup>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <ul> 
      <li>Some smartphones can be categorized as high-end <a href="/wiki/Point-and-shoot_camera" title="Point-and-shoot camera">point-and-shoot cameras</a> with large sensors up to 1" with 20 <a href="/wiki/Megapixel" title="Megapixel" class="mw-redirect">megapixels</a> and 4K video. Some can store their pictures in proprietary <a href="/wiki/Raw_image_format" title="Raw image format">raw image format</a>, but the Android (operating system) 5.0 Lollipop serves open source RAW images.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></li> 
      <li>In October 2015, Microsoft announced Windows Continuum, a feature that allows users to connect their devices to an external monitor via Microsoft Continuum Display Dock.<sup id="cite_ref-windows.microsoft.com_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-windows.microsoft.com-42">[42]</a></sup> HP adds a layer to the Continuum with their HP Workplace which enables user to run a Win32 app by a virtualized server.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Future_possible_developments">Future possible developments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Future possible developments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <ul> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Rollable_display" title="Rollable display">Foldable</a> OLED smartphones could be as much as a decade away because of the cost of producing them. There is a relatively high failure rate when producing these screens. As little as a speck of dust can ruin a screen during production. Creating a battery that can be folded is another hurdle.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Modular_smartphone" title="Modular smartphone">Modular smartphones</a> are projected, in which users can remove and replace parts.</li> 
      <li>Near future smartphones might not have a traditional battery as their sole source of power. Instead, they may pull energy from radio, television, cellular or Wi-Fi signals.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Mobile_operating_systems">Mobile operating systems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Mobile operating systems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Mobile_operating_system" title="Mobile operating system">Mobile operating system</a>
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Android">Android</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Android">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android (operating system)</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Android_6.0-en.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Android_6.0-en.png/170px-Android_6.0-en.png" width="170" height="302" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Android_6.0-en.png/255px-Android_6.0-en.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Android_6.0-en.png/340px-Android_6.0-en.png 2x" data-file-width="1080" data-file-height="1920"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Android_6.0-en.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Android 6.0 "Marshmallow" home screen (2015).
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p><i>Android</i> is an open-source platform founded in October 2003 by Andy Rubin and backed by Google, along with major hardware and software developers (such as <a href="/wiki/Intel" title="Intel">Intel</a>, <a href="/wiki/HTC_Corporation" title="HTC Corporation" class="mw-redirect">HTC</a>, <a href="/wiki/ARM_Holdings" title="ARM Holdings">ARM</a>, <a href="/wiki/Motorola" title="Motorola">Motorola</a>, <a href="/wiki/LG" title="LG" class="mw-redirect">LG</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Samsung" title="Samsung">Samsung</a>) that form the <a href="/wiki/Open_Handset_Alliance" title="Open Handset Alliance">Open Handset Alliance</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-open-alliance_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-open-alliance-26">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-android-atlas_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-android-atlas-27">[27]</a></sup> In October 2008, <a href="/wiki/HTC" title="HTC">HTC</a> released the HTC Dream, the execution of native applications and third-party apps which are available via <a href="/wiki/Google_Play" title="Google Play">Google Play</a>, which launched in October 2008 as <a href="/wiki/Android_Market" title="Android Market" class="mw-redirect">Android Market</a>. By Q4 2010, Android became the best-selling smartphone platform.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="iOS">iOS</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: iOS">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:IOS_9_Homescreen.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/dc/IOS_9_Homescreen.png/170px-IOS_9_Homescreen.png" width="170" height="302" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/dc/IOS_9_Homescreen.png/255px-IOS_9_Homescreen.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/d/dc/IOS_9_Homescreen.png 2x" data-file-width="270" data-file-height="480"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:IOS_9_Homescreen.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> iOS 9.1 home screen (2015).
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>iOS is a mobile operating system developed by Apple Inc. and distributed exclusively for Apple hardware. It is the operating system that powers the company's <a href="/wiki/IDevice" title="IDevice" class="mw-redirect">iDevices</a>. In 2007, Apple introduced the iPhone, the first device to use iOS and one of the first smartphones to use a multi-touch interface. The iPhone was notable for its use of a large touchscreen for direct finger input as its main means of interaction, instead of a stylus, keyboard, or keypad as typical for smartphones at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-iPhone-is-not_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iPhone-is-not-23">[23]</a></sup> In 2008, Apple introduced the <a href="/wiki/App_Store_(iOS)" title="App Store (iOS)">App Store</a>, which allowed any iPhone to install third-party native applications. Featuring over 500 applications at launch,<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> the App Store eventually achieved 1 billion downloads in the first year, and 75 billion by mid-2014.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> In January 2015, Apple announced that they have now sold one billion iOS devices.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Windows_Phone">Windows Phone</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Windows Phone">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Windows_Phone" title="Windows Phone">Windows Phone</a>
     </div> 
     <p>In 2010, Microsoft unveiled <a href="/wiki/Windows_Phone_7" title="Windows Phone 7">Windows Phone 7</a> with a <a href="/wiki/User_Interface" title="User Interface" class="mw-redirect">User Interface</a> inspired by Microsoft's "<a href="/wiki/Metro_Design_Language" title="Metro Design Language" class="mw-redirect">Metro Design Language</a>", to replace Windows Mobile. Windows Phone 7 integrates with Microsoft services such as <a href="/wiki/SkyDrive" title="SkyDrive" class="mw-redirect">Microsoft SkyDrive</a>, <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Office_Mobile" title="Microsoft Office Mobile">Office</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xbox" title="Xbox">Xbox</a> and <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Bing" title="Microsoft Bing" class="mw-redirect">Bing</a>, as well as non-Microsoft services such as <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a>, <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> and <a href="/wiki/Google_Account" title="Google Account">Google accounts</a>. This software platform runs the <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Mobile" title="Microsoft Mobile">Microsoft Mobile</a> smartphones, and has received some positive reception from the technology press and been praised for its uniqueness and differentiation.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> In 2012, Microsoft released <a href="/wiki/Windows_Phone_8" title="Windows Phone 8">Windows Phone 8</a>, replacing its previously Windows CE-based architecture with one based on the <a href="/wiki/Windows_NT" title="Windows NT">Windows NT</a> kernel with many components shared with <a href="/wiki/Windows_8" title="Windows 8">Windows 8</a>, allowing applications to be ported between the two platforms. In recent version of Windows Phone turn into new series called <a href="/wiki/Windows_10_Mobile" title="Windows 10 Mobile">Windows 10 Mobile</a> , They insert many new things like App porting from Android, iOS, a brand new mobile computing called Windows Continuum which allow users to use full-fledged PC experience by putting a Display, Keyboard and mouse. Also a new <a href="/wiki/Universal_Windows_Platform" title="Universal Windows Platform">Universal Windows Platform</a> has announced by which developer can build any app for every Windows 10 platform with same core API. This version of Windows Phone have lot of things for developers.<sup id="cite_ref-windows.microsoft.com_42-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-windows.microsoft.com-42">[42]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:A_customized_homescreen_of_Windows_10_Mobile_(2015).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/A_customized_homescreen_of_Windows_10_Mobile_%282015%29.jpg/170px-A_customized_homescreen_of_Windows_10_Mobile_%282015%29.jpg" width="170" height="303" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/A_customized_homescreen_of_Windows_10_Mobile_%282015%29.jpg/256px-A_customized_homescreen_of_Windows_10_Mobile_%282015%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/A_customized_homescreen_of_Windows_10_Mobile_%282015%29.jpg/341px-A_customized_homescreen_of_Windows_10_Mobile_%282015%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="540" data-file-height="960"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:A_customized_homescreen_of_Windows_10_Mobile_(2015).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> A Customized Windows 10 Mobile's start screen.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="BlackBerry">BlackBerry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: BlackBerry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/BlackBerry" title="BlackBerry">BlackBerry</a>
     </div> 
     <p>In 1999, <a href="/wiki/Research_In_Motion" title="Research In Motion" class="mw-redirect">RIM</a> released its first BlackBerry devices, providing secure real-time push-email communications on wireless devices. Services such as BlackBerry Messenger provide the integration of all communications into a single inbox. In September 2012, RIM announced that the 200 millionth BlackBerry smartphone was shipped. As of September 2014, there are around 46 million active BlackBerry service subscribers.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> Most recently, RIM has undergone a platform transition, changing its name to BlackBerry and making new devices on a new platform named "BlackBerry 10"<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> and in November 2015 released an Android smartphone, the <a href="/wiki/BlackBerry_Priv" title="BlackBerry Priv">BlackBerry Priv</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Firefox_OS">Firefox OS</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Firefox OS">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Firefox_OS" title="Firefox OS">Firefox OS</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Firefox OS (originally called the <i>boot to gecko</i> project) was demonstrated by <a href="/wiki/Mozilla" title="Mozilla">Mozilla</a> in February 2012. It was designed to have a complete community based alternative system for mobile devices, using open standards and HTML5 applications. The first commercially available Firefox OS phones were ZTE Open and Alcatel One Touch Fire. As of 2014 more companies have partnered with Mozilla including Panasonic (which is making a smart TV with Firefox OS) and Sony.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sailfish_OS">Sailfish OS</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Sailfish OS">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Sailfish_OS" title="Sailfish OS">Sailfish OS</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The Sailfish OS is based on the <a href="/wiki/Linux_kernel" title="Linux kernel">Linux kernel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mer_(software_distribution)" title="Mer (software distribution)">Mer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> Additionally Sailfish OS includes a partially or completely <a href="/wiki/Proprietary_software" title="Proprietary software">proprietary</a> multi-tasking <a href="/wiki/User_interface" title="User interface">user interface</a> programmed by <a href="/wiki/Jolla" title="Jolla">Jolla</a>. This user interface differentiate Jolla smartphones from others.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> Sailfish OS is intended to be a system made by many of the MeeGo team, which left Nokia to form Jolla, utilizing funding from Nokia's "Bridge" program which helps establish and support start-up companies formed by ex-Nokia employees.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tizen">Tizen</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Tizen">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Tizen" title="Tizen">Tizen</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Tizen is a Linux-based <a href="/wiki/Operating_system" title="Operating system">operating system</a> for devices, including smartphones, <a href="/wiki/Tablet_computer" title="Tablet computer">tablets</a>, <a href="/wiki/In_car_entertainment" title="In car entertainment">in-vehicle infotainment</a> (IVI) devices, smart TVs, <a href="/wiki/Laptop" title="Laptop">laptops</a> and smart cameras. Tizen is a project within the <a href="/wiki/Linux_Foundation" title="Linux Foundation">Linux Foundation</a> and is governed by a Technical Steering Group (TSG) composed of Samsung and Intel among others. In April 2014, Samsung released the Samsung Gear 2 and the Gear 2 Neo, running Tizen.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Samsung_Z1" title="Samsung Z1">Samsung Z1</a> is the first smartphone produced by Samsung that runs Tizen; it was released in the <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">Indian</a> market on January 14, 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ubuntu_Touch">Ubuntu Touch</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Ubuntu Touch">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Ubuntu_Touch" title="Ubuntu Touch">Ubuntu Touch</a>
     </div> 
     <p><b>Ubuntu Touch</b> (also known as <b>Ubuntu Phone</b>) is a mobile version of the <a href="/wiki/Ubuntu_operating_system" title="Ubuntu operating system" class="mw-redirect">Ubuntu operating system</a> developed by <a href="/wiki/Canonical_Ltd" title="Canonical Ltd" class="mw-redirect">Canonical UK Ltd</a> and Ubuntu Community.<sup id="cite_ref-backed_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-backed-68">[68]</a></sup> It is designed primarily for touchscreen mobile devices such as smartphones and tablet computers.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Discontinued_mobile_operating_systems">Discontinued mobile operating systems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Discontinued mobile operating systems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Symbian">Symbian</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Symbian">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Symbian" title="Symbian">Symbian</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Symbian was originally developed by <a href="/wiki/Psion_(computers)" title="Psion (computers)" class="mw-redirect">Psion</a> as <a href="/wiki/EPOC32" title="EPOC32" class="mw-redirect">EPOC32</a>. It was the world's most widely used smartphone operating system until Q4 2010, though the platform never gained popularity or widespread awareness in the U.S., as it did in Europe and Asia. The first Symbian phone, the touchscreen Ericsson R380 Smartphone, was released in 2000,<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> and was the first device marketed as a "smartphone".<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> It combined a PDA with a mobile phone.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> In February 2011, Nokia announced that it would replace Symbian with Windows Phone as the operating system on all of its future smartphones, with the platform getting abandoned throughout the following few years.<sup id="cite_ref-NokiaWinPho7_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NokiaWinPho7-73">[73]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Windows_Mobile">Windows Mobile</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Windows Mobile">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Windows_Mobile" title="Windows Mobile">Windows Mobile</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Windows Mobile was based on the <a href="/wiki/Windows_CE" title="Windows CE">Windows CE</a> kernel and first appeared as the Pocket PC 2000 operating system. Throughout its lifespan, the operating system was available in both touchscreen and non-touchscreen formats. It was supplied with a suite of applications developed with the Microsoft Windows API and was designed to have features and appearance somewhat similar to desktop versions of Windows. Third parties could develop software for Windows Mobile with no restrictions imposed by Microsoft. Software applications were eventually purchasable from Windows Marketplace for Mobile during the service's brief lifespan. Windows Mobile was phased out in favor of Windows Phone.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bada">Bada</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Bada">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Bada" title="Bada">Bada</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The Bada operating system for smartphones was announced by Samsung in November 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> The first Bada-based phone was the <a href="/wiki/Samsung_S8500" title="Samsung S8500" class="mw-redirect">Samsung Wave S8500</a>, released in June 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> Samsung shipped 4.5 million phones running Bada in Q2 of 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> In 2013, Bada merged with a similar platform called Tizen.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Palm_OS">Palm OS</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Palm OS">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Palm_OS" title="Palm OS">Palm OS</a>
     </div> 
     <p>In late 2001, <a href="/wiki/Handspring_(company)" title="Handspring (company)">Handspring</a> launched the <a href="/wiki/Springboard_Expansion_Slot" title="Springboard Expansion Slot">Springboard</a> GSM phone module with limited success. In May 2002, Handspring released the Palm OS <a href="/wiki/Treo_270" title="Treo 270">Treo 270</a> smartphone, that did not support Springboard, with both a touchscreen and a full keyboard. The Treo had wireless web browsing, email, calendar, a contact organizer and mobile third-party applications that could be downloaded or synced with a computer.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> Handspring was purchased by <a href="/wiki/Palm,_Inc" title="Palm, Inc" class="mw-redirect">Palm, Inc</a> which released the <a href="/wiki/Treo_600" title="Treo 600">Treo 600</a> and continued releasing Treo devices with a few Treo devices using Windows Mobile. After buying Palm in 2011, Hewlett-Packard (HP) discontinued its webOS smartphone and tablet production.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="webOS">webOS</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: webOS">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/WebOS" title="WebOS">webOS</a> was from <a href="/wiki/LG" title="LG" class="mw-redirect">LG</a>, although some parts are open source. webOS is a proprietary mobile operating system running on the Linux kernel, initially developed by Palm, which launched with the <a href="/wiki/Palm_Pre" title="Palm Pre">Palm Pre</a>. After being acquired by HP, two phones (the <a href="/wiki/HP_Veer" title="HP Veer">Veer</a> and the <a href="/wiki/HP_Pre_3" title="HP Pre 3">Pre 3</a>) and a tablet (the <a href="/wiki/HP_TouchPad" title="HP TouchPad">TouchPad</a>) running webOS were introduced in 2011. On August 18, 2011, HP announced that webOS hardware was to be discontinued<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> but would continue to support and update webOS software and develop the webOS ecosystem.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> HP released webOS as open source under the name Open webOS, and plans to update it with additional features.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> On February 25, 2013 HP announced the sale of WebOS to LG Electronics, who planned to use the operating system for its "smart" or Internet-connected TVs. In January 2014, <a href="/wiki/Qualcomm" title="Qualcomm">Qualcomm</a> has announced that it has acquired technology patents from HP, which includes all the WebOS patents.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Application_stores">Application stores</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Application stores">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_digital_distribution_platforms_for_mobile_devices" title="List of digital distribution platforms for mobile devices" class="mw-redirect">List of digital distribution platforms for mobile devices</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The introduction of Apple's App Store for the iPhone and iPod Touch in July 2008 popularized manufacturer-hosted <a href="/wiki/List_of_digital_distribution_platforms_for_mobile_devices" title="List of digital distribution platforms for mobile devices" class="mw-redirect">online distribution</a> for third-party applications (<a href="/wiki/Software" title="Software">software</a>, <a href="/wiki/Computer_programs" title="Computer programs" class="mw-redirect">computer programs</a>) focused on a single platform. Up until that point, smartphone application distribution depended on <a href="/wiki/List_of_digital_distribution_platforms_for_mobile_devices#Third-party_platforms" title="List of digital distribution platforms for mobile devices" class="mw-redirect">third-party sources</a> providing applications for multiple platforms, such as <a href="/wiki/GetJar" title="GetJar">GetJar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Handango" title="Handango">Handango</a>, <a href="/wiki/Handmark" title="Handmark">Handmark</a>, and <a href="/wiki/PocketGear" title="PocketGear" class="mw-redirect">PocketGear</a>.</p> 
     <p>Following the success of the App Store, other smartphone manufacturers launched application stores, such as Google's Android Market in October 2008 and RIM's <a href="/wiki/BlackBerry_App_World" title="BlackBerry App World" class="mw-redirect">BlackBerry App World</a> in April 2009. In February 2014, 93% of <a href="/wiki/Mobile_developers" title="Mobile developers" class="mw-redirect">mobile developers</a> were targeting smartphones first for mobile app development.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Display">Display</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Display">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Display_device" title="Display device">Display device</a>
     </div> 
     <p>One of the main characteristics of smartphones is their <a href="/wiki/Display_device" title="Display device">screen</a>. It usually fills almost the entire phone surface (about 70%); screen size usually defines the size of a smartphone. Many have an aspect ratio of <a href="/wiki/4:3" title="4:3" class="mw-redirect">4:3</a> or <a href="/wiki/16:9" title="16:9">16:9</a>.</p> 
     <p>They are measured in diagonal <a href="/wiki/Inch" title="Inch">inches</a>, starting from 2.45 inches.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> Phones with screens larger than 5.2 inches are referred to as "<a href="/wiki/Phablet" title="Phablet">phablets</a>". Smartphones with screens over 4.5 inches commonly are moved around in the hand or used with both hands, since the average thumb cannot reach the entire screen surface. Types of screen include <a href="/w/index.php?title=IPS_OR_TN&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="IPS OR TN (page does not exist)">IPS OR TN</a> type <a href="/w/index.php?title=LED/CCFL_BACKLIT_LCD&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="LED/CCFL BACKLIT LCD (page does not exist)">LED/CCFL BACKLIT LCD</a>, OLED, <a href="/wiki/AMOLED" title="AMOLED">AMOLED</a>, e-INK display, etc.</p> 
     <p>An upcoming development is a <a href="/wiki/Braille" title="Braille">Braille</a> screen, using <a href="/wiki/Microfluidics" title="Microfluidics">microfluidics</a> technology.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Market_share">Market share</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Market share">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Smartphone_usage">Smartphone usage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Smartphone usage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <p>In the third quarter of 2012, one billion smartphones were in use worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> Global smartphone sales surpassed the sales figures for features phones in early 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-news1_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-news1-89">[89]</a></sup> As of 2013, 65 percent of U.S. mobile consumers own smartphones.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> The European mobile device market as of 2013 is 860 million.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> In China, smartphones represented more than half of all handset shipments in the second quarter of 2012<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> and in 2014 there were 519.7 million smartphone users, with the number estimated to grow to 700 million by 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>As of November 2011, 27% of all photographs were taken with camera-equipped smartphones.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> A study conducted in September 2012 concluded that 4 out of 5 smartphone owners use the device to shop.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> Another study conducted in June 2013 concluded that 56% of American adults now owned a smartphone of some kind. Android and iPhone owners account for half of the cell phone user population. Higher income adults and those under age 35 lead the way when it comes to smartphone ownership.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>Worldwide shipments of smartphones topped 1 billion units in 2013, up 38% from 2012's 725 million, while comprising a 55% share of the mobile phone market in 2013, up from 42% in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="By_manufacturer">By manufacturer</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: By manufacturer">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:341px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Smartphones_back.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Smartphones_back.jpg/339px-Smartphones_back.jpg" width="339" height="226" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Smartphones_back.jpg/509px-Smartphones_back.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Smartphones_back.jpg/678px-Smartphones_back.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456"></a>

        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Smartphones_back.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> Smartphone brands: LG, OnePlus, Samsung and Apple
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <table class="wikitable"> 
      <caption>

       </tr> 
      </tbody>
     </table> 
     <p>In 2011, Apple had the highest shipment <a href="/wiki/Market_share" title="Market share">market share</a> worldwide. In 2013, Samsung had 31.3% market share, a slight increase from 30.3% in 2012, while Apple was at 15.3%, a decrease from 18.7% in 2012. Huawei, LG and Lenovo were at about 5% each, significantly better than 2012 figures, while others had about 40%, the same as the previous years figure. Only Apple lost market share, although their shipment volume still increased by 12.9 percent; the rest had significant increases in shipment volumes of 36 to 92 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> In Q1 2014, Samsung had a 31% share and Apple had 16%.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> In Q4 2014, Apple had a 20.4% share and Samsung had 19.9%.<sup id="cite_ref-brett_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-brett-107">[107]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>In Q1 2015 in the US, Android market share was 53.2%; Apple's iPhone had a 41.3% share and Samsung's Android smartphones had 29.3%.<sup id="cite_ref-ComScore1_102-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ComScore1-102">[102]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="By_operating_system">By operating system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: By operating system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Mobile_operating_system" title="Mobile operating system">Mobile operating system</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The market has been dominated by the Android operating system since 2010. Android's market share (measured by units shipment) rose from 33.2% in Q4 2011 to 78.1% of the market in Q4 2013. Apple's market share oscillated between 15% to 20.9% during the same period. BlackBerry's market share fell from 14.3% in Q4 2011 to 0.6% in Q4 2013. Windows Mobile market share rose from 1.5% to 3% during the same time frame.<sup id="cite_ref-2014_market_share_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2014_market_share-108">[108]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>As of the end of Q3 2014, Android was the most popular operating system, with a 84.4% market share, followed by iOS with 11.7%, Windows Phone with 2.9%, BlackBerry with 0.5% and all others with 0.6%.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup></p> 
     <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_sales_figures.2C_in_millions">Historical sales figures, in millions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Historical sales figures, in millions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Issues">Issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <p>Smartphones have presented issues besides those affecting other <a href="/wiki/Mobile_telephone" title="Mobile telephone" class="mw-redirect">mobile telephones</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Battery_life">Battery life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Battery life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:USB_battery_charger.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/USB_battery_charger.jpg/220px-USB_battery_charger.jpg" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/USB_battery_charger.jpg/330px-USB_battery_charger.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/USB_battery_charger.jpg/440px-USB_battery_charger.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4314" data-file-height="3096"></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:USB_battery_charger.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
        </div> A high-capacity portable battery charger.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Compared to earlier non-smartphones, smartphone battery life has generally been poor and a significant drain on customer satisfaction.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Social">Social</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Social">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Smartphone_addiction" title="Smartphone addiction" class="mw-redirect">Smartphone addiction</a>
     </div> 
     <p>A 2012 <a href="/wiki/University_of_Southern_California" title="University of Southern California">University of Southern California</a> study found that <a href="/wiki/Safe_sex" title="Safe sex">unprotected</a> <a href="/wiki/Adolescent_sexuality" title="Adolescent sexuality">adolescent sexual</a> activity was more common among owners of smartphones.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> A study conducted by the <a href="/wiki/Rensselaer_Polytechnic_Institute" title="Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute">Rensselaer Polytechnic Institute</a>'s (RPI) Lighting Research Center (LRC) concluded that smartphones, or any backlit devices, can seriously affect <a href="/wiki/Stages_of_sleep" title="Stages of sleep" class="mw-redirect">sleep cycles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Colaner_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colaner-120">[120]</a></sup> Some persons might become psychologically attached to cellphones resulting in anxiety when separated from the devices.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>A "<a href="/wiki/Smombie" title="Smombie">smombie</a>" (a combination of "smartphone" and "<a href="/wiki/Zombie" title="Zombie">zombie</a>") is a walking person using a smartphone and not paying attention as they walk, possibly risking an accident in the process, an increasing social phenomenon.<sup id="cite_ref-sunday-times_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sunday-times-122">[122]</a></sup> The issue of slow-moving mobile phone users has led to the creation of a "mobile lane" for walking in the city of <a href="/wiki/Chongqing" title="Chongqing">Chongqing</a>, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-123">[123]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal">Legal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Legal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Smartphone_wars" title="Smartphone wars" class="mw-redirect">Smartphone wars</a>
     </div> 
     <p>A "patent war" between Samsung and Apple started when the latter claimed that the original <a href="/wiki/Samsung_Galaxy_S" title="Samsung Galaxy S">Galaxy S</a> Android phone copied the interfaceand possibly the hardwareof Apple's iOS for the <a href="/wiki/IPhone_3GS" title="IPhone 3GS">iPhone 3GS</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medical">Medical</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Medical">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Mobile_app" title="Mobile app">Mobile app</a>
     </div> 
     <p>With the rise in number of mobile medical apps in the market place, government regulatory agencies raised concerns on the safety of the use of such applications. These concerns were transformed into regulation initiatives worldwide with the aim of safeguarding users from untrusted medical advice.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Security">Security</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Security">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles: 
      <a href="/wiki/Mobile_security" title="Mobile security">Mobile security</a>, 
      <a href="/wiki/Malware" title="Malware">Malware</a>, 
      <a href="/wiki/Mobile_virus" title="Mobile virus">Mobile virus</a> and 
      <a href="/wiki/Media_Transfer_Protocol" title="Media Transfer Protocol">Media Transfer Protocol</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Smartphone malware is easily distributed through an insecure <a href="/wiki/App_store" title="App store">app store</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Juniper-malware_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Juniper-malware-125">[125]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-trustbus11_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trustbus11-126">[126]</a></sup> Often malware is hidden in <a href="/wiki/Copyright_infringement_of_software" title="Copyright infringement of software" class="mw-redirect">pirated</a> versions of legitimate apps, which are then distributed through third-party app stores.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> Malware risk also comes from what's known as an "update attack", where a legitimate application is later changed to include a malware component, which users then install when they are notified that the app has been updated.<sup id="cite_ref-Lookout-malware_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lookout-malware-129">[129]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>One out of three robberies in 2012 in the United States involved the theft of a mobile phone. An online petition has urged smartphone makers to install <a href="/wiki/Kill_switch" title="Kill switch">kill switches</a> in their devices.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> In 2014, Apple's "Find my iPhone" and Google's "Android Device Manager" can disable phones that have been lost/stolen. With BlackBerry Protect in OS version 10.3.2, devices can be rendered unrecoverable to even BlackBerry's own Operating System recovery tools if incorrectly authenticated or dissociated from their account.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sleep">Sleep</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Sleep">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
     <div role="note" class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Sleep#Stages" title="Sleep">Sleep  Stages</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Using smartphones late at night can disturb sleep, due to the brightly lit screen affecting <a href="/wiki/Melatonin" title="Melatonin">melatonin</a> levels and <a href="/wiki/Sleep_cycles" title="Sleep cycles" class="mw-redirect">sleep cycles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_terms">Other terms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Other terms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <p>"<a href="/wiki/Phablet" title="Phablet">Phablet</a>", a <a href="/wiki/Portmanteau" title="Portmanteau">portmanteau</a> of the words <i>phone</i> and <i>tablet</i>, describes smartphones with larger screens.<sup id="cite_ref-forbes_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forbes-136">[136]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pcmag_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pcmag-137">[137]</a></sup></p> 
     <p>"Superphone" is also used by some companies to market phones with unusually large screens and other expensive features.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Smartphone&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <div class="noprint portal tright" style="border:solid #aaa 1px;margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em">

     </div>
